        "issue": "Conventional high-rise residential towers often separate residents from nature, create hard urban facades, increase exposure to sunlight and heat, and contribute little to urban biodiversity.",
        "concept": "Transform the high-rise residential tower into a vertical forest, where balcony planting, vegetation, and ecological systems become part of everyday domestic life and urban green infrastructure.",
        "strategy": "Use projecting balconies as planting platforms, distribute trees and shrubs vertically across the facade, integrate irrigation and maintenance systems, and arrange vegetation according to orientation and seasonal conditions.",

        "issue": "High-rise residential towers often become anonymous, repetitive, and visually uniform. In dense luxury markets, residents also seek individuality, private outdoor space, large views, and distinctive domestic identity within the tower.",
        "concept": "Create a tower as a vertical stack of individualized homes, where each apartment becomes a pixel in the overall form and contributes to the building's irregular skyline identity.",
        "strategy": "Organize apartments around a compact central core, vary floor plate shapes and unit types across the height of the tower, use cantilevers and setbacks to create private terraces, and allow apartment variation to directly generate the pixelated facade and skyline silhouette.",
